Then Lessa hatched a daring and dangerous scheme to rally support from people who had long ago ceased to exist!</span>

<a href="/user/show/48104685-jean-rice" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1445360122i/48104685._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>

<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/48104685-jean-rice">Jean Rice</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Silver, it's not fantasy, it is science fiction. Dragons are genetically engineered and the people are colonists from Earth. It's right there in the<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Silver, it's not fantasy, it is science fiction. Dragons are genetically engineered and the people are colonists from Earth. It's right there in the prologue. All of the prequels deal with how they lost their technology over 2,500 years, and the sequels deal with reclaiming their technology.<br /><br />The author has said that the books are "science fiction with a fantasy element." <a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It depends how 'little' we are talking here. I completely disagree with the previous comment. This could be perfectly fine for a mature 12-year-old<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It depends how 'little' we are talking here. I completely disagree with the previous comment. This could be perfectly fine for a mature 12-year-old that enjoys fantasy. It was *not* written for children though, and does include sexual themes throughout. That being said, at 12 I was sneaking my mom's harlequin romances, so this was very tame. <a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_8907691">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8907691" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/545336-mike" class="left imgcol" title="Mike"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1329191662p2/545336.jpg" alt="Mike" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/8907691?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/545336-mike" class="user" title="Mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1132538.Dragonflight" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345247766" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=xcharity-2011" class="actionLinkLite">xcharity-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8907691">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12326981496382230476">What a disappointment. It started out just fine with Lessa, sole survivor of her family wreaking revenge on the evil dude who conquered "Ruatha Hold". The whole dragon/human mind meld thing was okay too. The part that really disgusted me was the whole raping/physical abuse shtick by the supposed hero. My thoughts were, if this was my daughter as the heroine, then the only thing to be done would "bag and tag" that F'lar a**hole cause I would have invented the .45 cal and then blown his head off w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12326981496382230476">What a disappointment. It started out just fine with Lessa, sole survivor of her family wreaking revenge on the evil dude who conquered "Ruatha Hold". The whole dragon/human mind meld thing was okay too. The part that really disgusted me was the whole raping/physical abuse shtick by the supposed hero. My thoughts were, if this was my daughter as the heroine, then the only thing to be done would "bag and tag" that F'lar a**hole cause I would have invented the .45 cal and then blown his head off with it. I don't get why this was important to the storyline, gee abuse the girl long enough and she'll fall for you in the end. Frankly thought it was stupid.<br /><br />Another thing that r'ally ann'yed me was the st'pid ap'strophe w'y to sp'll ev'ryone's friggin' n'mes!!! I want to pour scalding hot <em>klah</em> on the whole bunch.<br /><br />The premise that the world forgets, within a few years, a recurring extraterrestrial threat that destroys entire continents was idiotic. If they really forget the whole technological base that enabled them to defeat the "threads", the whole society deserves to perish. And "threads" are not a very exciting enemy, "wow, look at them falling from the sky in clumps..." <br /><br />Dialogue sucks mostly. Toward the end, there were parts where somebody "roared" with laughter, but I never saw anything remotely funny to cause it.<br /><br />I was really looking forward to a long and interesting series but not here. Good thing I didn't buy any of the follow-on's. I may have a tough time starting some of her other novels I have on the "to-read" list.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12326981496382230476">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1252445">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1252445" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/86946-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1374246859p2/86946.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1252445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/86946-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345284266" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/86946-jessica?shelf=re-reads" class="actionLinkLite">re-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1252445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4175120994167232321">It should be stated that I squandered most of junior high reading Anne McCaffrey's sci-fi/fantasy novels near-exclusively, but this was my first time revisiting her since then. I was surprised to find that the first book in the <em>Dragonriders of Pern</em> series actually does have a good story, with interesting characters and an excellent invented world. However, the writing is just abominable, and in spite of being a woman, McCaffrey is frustratingly chauvanistic. The (lack of) copyediting makes me cr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4175120994167232321">It should be stated that I squandered most of junior high reading Anne McCaffrey's sci-fi/fantasy novels near-exclusively, but this was my first time revisiting her since then. I was surprised to find that the first book in the <em>Dragonriders of Pern</em> series actually does have a good story, with interesting characters and an excellent invented world. However, the writing is just abominable, and in spite of being a woman, McCaffrey is frustratingly chauvanistic. The (lack of) copyediting makes me cry, and the writing is something you just have to suffer through, but the idea is really inventive, and I can totally understand how I got so sucked into her books as a kid. I wouldn't exactly recommend that you run out and check her books out, but if you liked them back in the day, revisiting them isn't as painful as you might have thought it would be.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_57047824">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57047824" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="left imgcol" title="Brad"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" alt="Brad" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/57047824?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1022982-brad" class="user" title="Brad">Brad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer57047824">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12211273492584046152">Lately I have been noticing a recurring observation about the quality of first books in various series. There seems to be a growing consensus in reviews that the first book of a series, particularly if it is the first book published by an author, is inherently weak because the author is "learning their craft."<br /><br />It seems to be both an excuse for what is perceived as poor quality and an excuse for going on in the series despite being underwhelmed by the opener. <br /><br />I had this in mind as I began reading</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12211273492584046152">Lately I have been noticing a recurring observation about the quality of first books in various series. There seems to be a growing consensus in reviews that the first book of a series, particularly if it is the first book published by an author, is inherently weak because the author is "learning their craft."<br /><br />It seems to be both an excuse for what is perceived as poor quality and an excuse for going on in the series despite being underwhelmed by the opener. <br /><br />I had this in mind as I began reading <a title="Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">Anne McCaffrey</a>'s <a title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_">Dragonflight</a>, and for two thirds of the book I thought it was a perfect descriptor of what I was seeing. <br /><br />But once I finished the book, I thought that maybe "the poor opener" isn't always the case (although I willingly concede that this is probably the case more often than not). Perhaps there is something else going on -- especially in something like Dragonflight.<br /><br />Dragonflight is a fast read, and it is sparingly written. We get a taste of the main characters -- F'lar and Mnementh, Lessa and Ramoth, F'nor and Canth -- but we aren't given much time with them, not enough to get to know them deeply. McCaffrey races us through the story, spanning many Turns (the Pernese year) in a very short time. There is a clear goal to her plot -- save Pern from the threat of the Threads -- and McCaffrey is ruthless and expedient in getting us there. <br /><br />I can understand how many readers see this as a narrative failure. After all, we like getting to know characters in the books we read, and we seem to prefer saving our breathless action driven stories for the big screen. <br /><br />If this is our preference, a story which focuses on the latter rather than the former has failed on some level, and that failure is generally considered the writer's failure and, more specifically, a failure of their writing. <br /><br />I wonder, though, if this is always the case. It seems to me that it is just as likely that Dragonflight's quickness could have more to do with the peculiarities of its publishing (it was two novellas squished together to make a novel), the requirements of a first time writer to get their work just right so that it can be published at all (which often means cutting out superfluities), and the tendency of first books to be edited more thoroughly than future books. <br /><br />Once you've become "Anne McCaffrey," for instance, editors tend to step back and give you more room. They let you spend many more ages on character building, and you're given less notes on your work. You are "Anne McCaffrey," best selling author, and you must know what you're doing, so do what you want.<br /><br />Perhaps then, <a title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_">Dragonflight</a> is a product of the necessities of a first novel rather than an example of the author not being polished in her writing skills.<br /><br />All this aside, I appreciated the quickness of the tale. There is something to be said for brevity, and I felt I got enough of the characters. I cared about them without knowing everything, and some of their shabbier behaviours -- such as F'lar's constant physical abuse of Lessa, and Lessa's infuriating capacity for inspired stupidity -- were more tolerable than they might have been if I'd been forced to spend time digging through their psychologies. <br /><br />Of course, this appreciation for skeletal characterization could all be the screenwriter in me (I doubt it, though, since the main complaint about my screenplays by those with the money is that they are too character driven), but that's okay because that informs the kind of reader I can be. Every once in a while I like my stories quick and my characters less defined (although this is far from always the case), and <a title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_">Dragonflight</a> fit that bill right when I needed it most.<br /><br />Regardless, <a title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_">Dragonflight</a> was a surprise for me, and I liked it much more than I thought I would. I don't know if I will go on, though. I may just let it stand alone, enjoying its quality as is. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12211273492584046152">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_54622660">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54622660" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1803452-libby" class="left imgcol" title="Libby"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1248364924p2/1803452.jpg" alt="Libby" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/54622660?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1803452-libby" class="user" title="Libby">Libby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=read-in-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=fantasy-epic-and-series" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-epic-and-series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=fantasy-fairytale-and-myth" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-fairytale-and-myth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer54622660">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16945442132020922666">I truly enjoyed this book and am looking forward to continuing with the series. This work is a well-written, creative adventure novel with the perfect amount of romance. It’s storytelling at its best. <br /><br />The book is a nice mix of Science Fiction and Fantasy. The setting is the world of Pern. We are told in the Prologue that Pern is a planet settled by Earthlings but now long forgotten. It has apparently reverted back to a feudal type society where most of the citizens live in “holds” which are hist</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16945442132020922666">I truly enjoyed this book and am looking forward to continuing with the series. This work is a well-written, creative adventure novel with the perfect amount of romance. It’s storytelling at its best. <br /><br />The book is a nice mix of Science Fiction and Fantasy. The setting is the world of Pern. We are told in the Prologue that Pern is a planet settled by Earthlings but now long forgotten. It has apparently reverted back to a feudal type society where most of the citizens live in “holds” which are historically protected by “Weyrs”. The biggest threat facing Pern is environmental; the Threads fall from a neighboring planet and destroy all organic matter on Pern. For centuries the Dragonmen, residents of the Weyrs, have used their dragons to sear the Threads out of the sky before they can infect Pern. But now, over 400 years have passed without any Threads falling and the people of Pern believe the danger is over and that the Dragonmen have outlived their purpose. Too late, we find out that failing to maintain and believe in tradition has weakened the people of Pern and there are dire consequences when the Threads return.<br /><br />I’ve seen a lot of criticism here that the book lacks character development and/or that the main romantic relationship is sexist and abusive etc. I do agree that this book is somewhat dated and that how writers represent romantic relationships has certainly altered to reflect the current social norms. However, I think the romantic relationship between F’lar and Lessa, while dated, is not outright abusive. As the setting of the book is feudal, I think the male dominate culture is appropriate. Further, much of this resolves as you see their relationship evolve over the course of the book into a relationship of equals. All that aside, this is a Sci/Fi / Fantasy novel not a dating manual. I find it odd that readers expect to see healthy, politically correct relationships and/or that they expect people to emulate the relationships they read about in books; if that’s true so much for Wuthering Heights. The relationship fits the setting and works for the novel. I think people may read too much into it. <br /><br />The highlight of this book for me is the amazing relationship between a rider and his/her dragon. Once a dragon Impresses a rider they are forever two parts of one whole. The relationship is unique and moving. It’s a great companion aspect to the fast paced and engaging plot. I’d recommend this to anyone who enjoys a book that is a lighter read while still being a richly told adventure story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16945442132020922666">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven" class="user" title="David Sven">David Sven</a>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer576058030">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3724221541133378160">A quick and easy read. The world building is light with a lot of unanswered questions, but I'm assured that the series as a whole "fills out" in that regard. I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The prologue had me doing a double take because it was pure scifi, with Pern being one of many colonised planets which eventually became isolated and forgotten by Earth. The technology then regressed to the more fantasy feel medieval style setting. There are dragons, but even these are indigenous animals that have been bred to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3724221541133378160">A quick and easy read. The world building is light with a lot of unanswered questions, but I'm assured that the series as a whole "fills out" in that regard. I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The prologue had me doing a double take because it was pure scifi, with Pern being one of many colonised planets which eventually became isolated and forgotten by Earth. The technology then regressed to the more fantasy feel medieval style setting. There are dragons, but even these are indigenous animals that have been bred to resemble dragons of Earth mythology. There's no magic per se. Rather we have dragons with the ability to teleport and certain human blood lines are able to telepathically communicate and "bond" with the dragons.<br /><br />The dragons are bred to combat an invasion of "Threads," a life destroying "entity" or "organism" that travels from Pern's sister planet every two hundred years when the planets are closest in their orbits.<br /><br /><br />The story is set when there has been 400 years of no "Threads" and the dragons have been in decline. As the 200 year cycle comes around once more the queen dragon is dying and a new "Weyrwoman" is sought to bond with a new queen dragon before the "Threads" fall once again.<br /><br />It held my attention from start to finish. I'll probably read the next book in the series when I need a quick palate cleanser.<br /><br /><br />4 stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3724221541133378160">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/8304931?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 26, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/58925-steph" class="user" title="Steph">Steph</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8304931">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12552506694324050256">I read this book back in sixth grade and thought it was exciting in the "wow, dragons are so cool; I wish I had one!" sense. I read it again on a whim and found it unintentionally disturbing. It's not just that the writing seemed dry and the characterization wooden. I realize the book was written in the late 60's, but the male-female dynamics still seem uncomfortably dated. The text seems to condone F'lar's treatment of Lessa; he patronizes her, yells at her, shakes her when he's angry, and prac</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12552506694324050256">I read this book back in sixth grade and thought it was exciting in the "wow, dragons are so cool; I wish I had one!" sense. I read it again on a whim and found it unintentionally disturbing. It's not just that the writing seemed dry and the characterization wooden. I realize the book was written in the late 60's, but the male-female dynamics still seem uncomfortably dated. The text seems to condone F'lar's treatment of Lessa; he patronizes her, yells at her, shakes her when he's angry, and practically rapes her. She never confronts him about it. And then, plot aside, she's supposed to "come around" to love him in the end. I never noticed it when I was younger, but it troubles me now that this is supposed to feel romantic.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12552506694324050256">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_17575471">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17575471" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/138600-sean" class="left imgcol" title="Sean"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1323721629p2/138600.jpg" alt="Sean" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17575471?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 18, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/138600-sean" class="user" title="Sean">Sean</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17575471">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8925105084418004214">The Dragonriders of Pern series really caught my imagination back in my preteen/early-teen years, when I picked up a library copy of <a title="The Renegades of Pern (#7) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20082.The_Renegades_of_Pern___7___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__">The Renegades of Pern</a> that my mom had put down. I next read <a title="All The Weyrs Of Pern by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61926.All_The_Weyrs_Of_Pern">All the Weyrs of Pern</a> (thrilling at the brilliant cover art by Michael Whelan) and then started from the beginning, whipping through Dragonflight, <a title="Dragonquest (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 2) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127584.Dragonquest__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_2_">Dragonquest</a>, <a title="The White Dragon (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 3) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_3_">The White Dragon</a>, <a title="Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 4) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_4_">Moreta</a>, <a title="Nerilka's Story (#5) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61974.Nerilka_s_Story___5___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__">Nerilka's Story</a> and the <a title="Dragonsong (Harper Hall Trilogy, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28541.Dragonsong__Harper_Hall_Trilogy__Book_1_">Harper Hall Trilogy</a>.<br /><br />I recently had the urge to revisit those carefree years of meaningless scienc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8925105084418004214">The Dragonriders of Pern series really caught my imagination back in my preteen/early-teen years, when I picked up a library copy of <a title="The Renegades of Pern (#7) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20082.The_Renegades_of_Pern___7___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__">The Renegades of Pern</a> that my mom had put down. I next read <a title="All The Weyrs Of Pern by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61926.All_The_Weyrs_Of_Pern">All the Weyrs of Pern</a> (thrilling at the brilliant cover art by Michael Whelan) and then started from the beginning, whipping through Dragonflight, <a title="Dragonquest (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 2) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127584.Dragonquest__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_2_">Dragonquest</a>, <a title="The White Dragon (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 3) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_3_">The White Dragon</a>, <a title="Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 4) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_4_">Moreta</a>, <a title="Nerilka's Story (#5) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61974.Nerilka_s_Story___5___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__">Nerilka's Story</a> and the <a title="Dragonsong (Harper Hall Trilogy, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28541.Dragonsong__Harper_Hall_Trilogy__Book_1_">Harper Hall Trilogy</a>.<br /><br />I recently had the urge to revisit those carefree years of meaningless science fiction I enjoyed, and I picked the first three books up again, only to be shocked at how misogynistic, outdated and just plain badly written they were. I mean, I knew they were pulpy, guilty-pleasure-type stuff, but to create a strong female character like Lessa (psi powers! rides a dragon! stubborn! intelligent(?)!) and then pair her with F'lar, who treats her like a child, shakes her when she displeases him . . . and have them fall in love? What kind of nonsense is this?<br /><br />The problem is, as viciously sub-par as her prose, characterization and plotting are, McCaffrey's premise still enthralls me. Even though the idea of any number of dragons being able to keep the skies of an entire continent free of what amounts to a corrosive blizzard is thoroughgoing twaddle, I still can't stop thinking about it. Is an unwilling re-reading of <em>Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</em> in my future??</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8925105084418004214">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_857709734">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857709734" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17295220-alexa" class="left imgcol" title="Alexa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" alt="Alexa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/857709734?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17295220-alexa" class="user" title="Alexa">Alexa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer857709734">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1127171709293448053">Around 2.5 stars. <br /><br /><strong>This book's prologue is terrible. </strong><br /><br />It's an opening narration supposed to serve (as they usually do) as an introduction to the story. However, it feels like an unnecessary info dump, placed there because apparently readers are too stupid to figure stuff out on their own and need to be spoon fed all the important facts.<br /><br />From then on things weren't <em>that</em> bad. The story is easy to read and I found the mix of Sci Fi/Fantasy really interesting. But the plot has holes and coincidences an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1127171709293448053">Around 2.5 stars. <br /><br /><strong>This book's prologue is terrible. </strong><br /><br />It's an opening narration supposed to serve (as they usually do) as an introduction to the story. However, it feels like an unnecessary info dump, placed there because apparently readers are too stupid to figure stuff out on their own and need to be spoon fed all the important facts.<br /><br />From then on things weren't <em>that</em> bad. The story is easy to read and I found the mix of Sci Fi/Fantasy really interesting. But the plot has holes and coincidences and ex-machina moments everywhere... I lost count of the times when I said: <em>"That should have gone wrong."</em> It never did.<br /><br />One of the things that bothered me the most was the absence of female characters. Actually, the absence of females. The dragonriders live with a group of people that supports them, and most of the riders come from the boys these families have. Now, unless otherwise stated, probability of having a girl or a boy is 50/50, which means there should be as many girls as boys in the weyr. However, when they need a dragonwoman or whatever the name was, they have to go search the outside world for girls... What happened to the ones they should have had in the Weyr? No one knows.<br /><br />Overall it wasn't as bad as other "classics" of the genre that I have read, but I don't think I'll be continuing with the series. <br /><br />Also, let it be known that ad'ding stu'pid apostrophes eve'rywhere doesn't make your nam'es more interes'ting. :/<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1127171709293448053">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer121100743">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5663660782254760824">10/2014 Buddy Reread: Reliving my preteen years with Don<br /><br /><strong> <blockquote>Once relieved of imminent danger, Pern settled into a more comfortable way of life. The descendants of heroes fell into disfavor, as the legends fell into disrepute.</blockquote> </strong><br /><br />Hooray! This book was as good as I remembered. The Pern books had a huge influence on my preadolescent self and I was a little nervous about rereading it and finding out that it wasn't as good. Afraid that it would destroy the related memories I made while reading these storie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5663660782254760824">10/2014 Buddy Reread: Reliving my preteen years with Don<br /><br /><strong>
  <blockquote>Once relieved of imminent danger, Pern settled into a more comfortable way of life. The descendants of heroes fell into disfavor, as the legends fell into disrepute.</blockquote>
</strong><br /><br />Hooray! This book was as good as I remembered. The Pern books had a huge influence on my preadolescent self and I was a little nervous about rereading it and finding out that it wasn't as good. Afraid that it would destroy the related memories I made while reading these stories. Best part, it felt like I was with my father again.<br /><br />Totally forgot how much of a pistol-whip Lessa was. Holy crackers. Headstrong, temperamental and willing to sacrifice herself and others to achieve a goal. Plus, a nice wide streak of vengeance runs through her. She's capable and don't f@#K with her. <br /><br />Glad to say, F'lar and F'nor were still the heartthrobs I recalled. While I respect F'lar's leadership and dedication, his interpersonal habits would drive me nuts. F'nor on the other hand, is so close to a perfect male for me that I still idolize him. <br /><br />The dragons. Mnementh... *deep sigh* If one could love a dragon, then this would be The One. Clever, loyal, acerbic wit and practically perfect in every way. Probably my favorite character in the story. <br /><br />Loved the revenge, Lessa's intrepidness, the mating flight, the harper ballads, and the politics of Pern. I adored Masterharper Robinton's scathing speech at the assembly--definitely need to reread the Harper Hall trilogy. F'lar maneuverings were brilliant and F'nor's loyalty and support--sexy. <strong>
  <blockquote>"I don’t object to being . . . importuned, but there are limits to what a man is willing to do out of loyalty to dragon kind.”</blockquote>
</strong><br />Still a great adventure story and I wish I could find transport to Pern. <br /><br />Favorite quote:<strong>
  <blockquote>“By the Egg, it’s die slow, doing nothing, or die quick, trying."</blockquote>
</strong></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_581496700">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581496700" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1669785-alex-ristea" class="left imgcol" title="Alex Ristea"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1413575351p2/1669785.jpg" alt="Alex Ristea" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/581496700?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1669785-alex-ristea" class="user" title="Alex Ristea">Alex Ristea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345284266" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=library" class="actionLinkLite">library</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=mmpb" class="actionLinkLite">mmpb</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=sword-laser" class="actionLinkLite">sword-laser</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1669785-alex-ristea?shelf=read-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-2013</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer581496700">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14722743989180806177">Dragonflight is a "classic" (take that definition as you will) that merits a read, even if that's just to understand the history of the genre a bit better.<br /><br />The best part of the book was undoubtedly McCaffrey's dragon imagery—anything that had to do with the their relationship with their riders, the feeling of them taking flight, or their general mannerisms. I wish I had picked this up in my younger days, as I'm sure the dragons alone would have captivated my fledgling mind, and I would have soake</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14722743989180806177">Dragonflight is a "classic" (take that definition as you will) that merits a read, even if that's just to understand the history of the genre a bit better.<br /><br />The best part of the book was undoubtedly McCaffrey's dragon imagery—anything that had to do with the their relationship with their riders, the feeling of them taking flight, or their general mannerisms. I wish I had picked this up in my younger days, as I'm sure the dragons alone would have captivated my fledgling mind, and I would have soaked it all in.<br /><br />Let's be honest, dragons are awe-inspiring and pretty fucking cool, so that alone should make you want to read this book.<br /><br />But I have to say that as far as characters and plot go, I wasn't particularly impressed. I've gotten so used to the character-driven fantasy novels written within the last decade or so that it's hard for me to digest books like Dragonflight.<br /><br />It just wasn't emotional enough for me.<br /><br />(And not of the cheesy, YA variety, but simply: the give-o-fuck factor of this book was too damn low. I wasn't invested at all.)<br /><br />POVs weren't tight enough for me to care about any character (don't get me started on how they hopped around willy-nilly within scenes), and the plot moves forward in time so quickly that there was no real opportunity to build any tension.<br /><br />I enjoyed some of the concepts and the dragons throughout, but I'm sorry to say that I won't be continuing with this series. 1968 literature is just not for me.<br /><br /><em>Two minor quirks to end this off. 1. I wish I would have started a count of how many times Lessa was shaken. Poor girl. 2. No offense, Anne McCaffrey, legend that you are, but what kind of evil name is the "Threads?" That doesn't evoke anything resembling impending doom, I'm sorry.</em><br /><br />PS There's a whole sexism debate I'm not even going to try to get into. For that, check out the discussions on the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170">Sword &amp; Laser</a> group, because Dragonflight is the April 2013 book club pick.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_242400274">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242400274" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2457095-apatt" class="left imgcol" title="Apatt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" alt="Apatt" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/242400274?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 06, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2457095-apatt" class="user" title="Apatt">Apatt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer242400274">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3461530115489036252">I read a few Pern books in my teen, I thought they were readable but at the time I was not all that taken with them. At that age I was not too discerning, I cared nothing for characterization, dialogue or prose. I read only for fun and escapism, not for the artistry of the works. Well, I am way out of my teen now, and I have cultivated an appreciation <em>finesse</em> to compensate for my own deficiency in that department.<br /><br />Since her recent passing tributes have been pouring in for Anne McCaffrey from nume</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3461530115489036252">I read a few Pern books in my teen, I thought they were readable but at the time I was not all that taken with them. At that age I was not too discerning, I cared nothing for characterization, dialogue or prose. I read only for fun and escapism, not for the artistry of the works. Well, I am way out of my teen now, and I have cultivated an appreciation <em>finesse</em> to compensate for my own deficiency in that department.<br /><br />Since her recent passing tributes have been pouring in for Anne McCaffrey from numerous quarters, including major sf/f writers including Neil Gaiman, David Brin, Lev Grossman, and Vonda McIntyre. These tributes reminded that I never really gave Anne McCaffrey's books a fair chance. Now is as good a time as any to start exploring them in earnest.<br /><br />When I first heard about this series decades ago the idea of fighting threads did not fill me with enthusiasm, I mean fighting <em>threads</em>? May as well fight balls of yarn! I thought. Ah, but then there are threads and there are <strong>Threads</strong>, these things are more menacing than I ever gave them any credit for. They are basically mindless, true, but so are zombies and the threads are even more deadly. They burn and they burrow and they are of course relentless<br /><br />This is not a YA book, it is not action packed, those looking for heart pounding scenes of dragon conflagration are not likely to be satisfied. The major strength and enduring popularity of this book - and I imagine the entire series - is the immersiveness of Pern. The slower chapters depicting day to life on Pern is what makes the world realistic, after all life is not full of nonstop action on a daily basis. The author wants you to live with her characters not go on missions with them. That said she really makes you wait for the threads to make an appearance though! The author's meticulous attention to details is awe inspiring.<br /><br />This is also not a fantasy book, not in the sense that Lord of the Rings or The Wheel of Time are. Anne herself has always been adamant that she is a science fiction author, no disrespect to the wonderful fantasy genre of course, but she deliberately backed the Pern fantasy tropes of dragons and medieval life with science. Pern is a planet, the dragons are genetically engineered and the lack of technology is due to some event that caused a fall of technological civilization. So no magic, no elves, no unicorns and no Dark Lord with a funny name (thank gawd!). Any way, what label you stick on a book does not matter, especially for a book of this calibre.<br /><br />Anne's prose style is - as her legions of fans would attest - is beautiful, clean, clear, concise and literary. The main characters are skillfully fleshed out, unfortunately my one complaint is that the protagonist Lessa is unrelentingly ill-tempered and willful to the point of being a pain in the posterior. I am looking forward to many more visits to Pern.<br /><br /><em>"That was well flown, I say. Well flown".</em><br />R.I.P. Anne.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3461530115489036252">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_122821096">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122821096" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2650335-sandra" class="left imgcol" title="Sandra"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1319863717p2/2650335.jpg" alt="Sandra" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/122821096?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 11, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2650335-sandra" class="user" title="Sandra">Sandra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11537309-dragonflight" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2650335-sandra?shelf=pnr-uf" class="actionLinkLite">pnr-uf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2650335-sandra?shelf=library-books" class="actionLinkLite">library-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2650335-sandra?shelf=shifters" class="actionLinkLite">shifters</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2650335-sandra?shelf=dragons" class="actionLinkLite">dragons</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2650335-sandra?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer122821096">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7145832510301744528">As this book was written in 1968, I'm sure everything that could be said, has been said. I'm just amazed at Anne McCaffrey's skill in crafting such a wonderful book. It feels as fresh as the day it was written.<br /><br />This is the story of the planet Pern, dragons, dragonryders, and Threads that come from the Red Star every couple of hundred years.<br /><br />No heavy world building here, just the world as is. As of course, it really must be! <br /><br />I want a dragon of my own, right now! <br /><br />Love this book and I'll be reading m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7145832510301744528">As this book was written in 1968, I'm sure everything that could be said, has been said. I'm just amazed at Anne McCaffrey's skill in crafting such a wonderful book. It feels as fresh as the day it was written.<br /><br />This is the story of the planet Pern, dragons, dragonryders, and Threads that come from the Red Star every couple of hundred years.<br /><br />No heavy world building here, just the world as is. As of course, it really must be! <br /><br />I want a dragon of my own, right now! <br /><br />Love this book and I'll be reading more of Anne McCaffrey's work :)<br /><br />Thanks Rivka for the inspiration ;)<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7145832510301744528">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_563197475">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563197475" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18438835-callum" class="left imgcol" title="Callum"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381804049p2/18438835.jpg" alt="Callum" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/563197475?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18438835-callum" class="user" title="Callum">Callum</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345284266" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=science-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">science-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=dragons" class="actionLinkLite">dragons</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=disappointing" class="actionLinkLite">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer563197475">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11878026032735907596"><strong>2.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />It wasn't difficult for me to ply myself in nineteen-seventies science fiction fantasy. The retro-singularity enmeshed with a keen sense of aesthetic majesty made for a more resplendent piece, yet I found very seldom to enjoy in Dragonflight. Unfortunately, the strongest aspects of Dragonflight had little sway in progressing the story, as opposed to structuring the setting around it. <br /><br />I was particularly interested in the feminist appeal Anne McCaffrey would deluge but, surprisingly, ther</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11878026032735907596"><strong>2.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />It wasn't difficult for me to ply myself in nineteen-seventies science fiction fantasy. The retro-singularity enmeshed with a keen sense of aesthetic majesty made for a more resplendent piece, yet I found very seldom to enjoy in Dragonflight. Unfortunately, the strongest aspects of Dragonflight had little sway in progressing the story, as opposed to structuring the setting around it. <br /><br />I was particularly interested in the feminist appeal Anne McCaffrey would deluge but, surprisingly, there was very little feminist integrity to be found in this novella. Her heroine had little character, and was generally unlikable. She had no unique, idiosyncratic traits or irregularities in her personality nor did she have a distinctive attribute. The integrality of her being was the fact that she was a female (a gender which came scarcely to protagonists in novels of this ilk during that certain decade). <br /><br />Her role in the novella was meant merely to ameliorate an all ready flat story. And if it wasn't for the particular anomalous of her circumstance, I wouldn't think twice about her character. Her heroine, unlike nearly all characters of this genre, isn't adorned in gowns or dresses. However, it's going to take a lot more than a leather clad, dragon mounting, loudmouth wench to really display a true exemplary of her feminist ideals.<br /><br />It's a shame that this novel started off auspiciously, dealing with courtly intrigues and the economics of their intergalactic society, while also barefaced in her science fiction concepts. Whereas the second half was null; the plethora of throw-away characters and the ultimate diminishing of the story's pace. <br /><br />And though it may sound odd, but the <em>Dragonriders Guild</em> was boring. Oftentimes consisting of brutish, monomaniacal men bickering over every scrap of trivial shares and responsibilities. Even with the appearance of a woman no truly interesting initiative was taken, nor did the story turn for the better. It was only earlier in the novel, where erratic noblemen and denizens were shown visibly conflicted with their presence and then, there was a true dynamism in her story. <br /><br />What really ends up working for her story is the imagery. Science fiction fantasy is a sub genre that has garnered quite a bit of acclaim, its mainstream genesis being The Dying Earth. Its elaborate prose along with an effulgent physicality keep Dragonflight somewhat readable. However, what really shines are the concepts which are too technological to be fantasy, yet too flaky to be science fiction. This would include leaping time intervals and my favourite, the Red Star.<br /><br />Better than any antagonist Anne McCaffrey could ever have contrived, the Red Star is her crowning piece of brain candy. A rogue planet, whose passing of Pern subjects it to an alien exposure that plagues the entire planet. It is a strange and hostile pestilence, which was able to provide some thrills.<br /><br />However, this lack of conflict is too detrimental. The second half of the story was a surplus of excursions that were revealed through brief conversations, and long-winded chapters which contained very little importance to the story as a whole. And though some intriguing concepts were explored, the lack of conflict left me completely apathetic. <br /><br />It's always upsetting to see a novel with tons of potential, squandered with poor storytelling. And in this case, her qualms festered in her characters as well. Her story, for better and worse, lacked a formulaic style that both plagued and enhanced Dragonflight. McCaffrey's concept was appealing and better yet, memorable. But the true helm of any novel lies in characterization and story, both of which ended up lacking.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11878026032735907596">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_482373432">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482373432" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4026072-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428797152p2/4026072.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/482373432?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 19, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4026072-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6327222-dragonflight" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=action" class="actionLinkLite">action</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=2013-literary-exploration-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">2013-literary-exploration-challenge</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=hugo-winner" class="actionLinkLite">hugo-winner</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=nebula-winner" class="actionLinkLite">nebula-winner</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=female-author" class="actionLinkLite">female-author</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=1960s" class="actionLinkLite">1960s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=book-club-sword-and-laser" class="actionLinkLite">book-club-sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=book-club-scifi-and-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">book-club-scifi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer482373432">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5221584678807613311">When something mentions fantasy/sci-fi and dragons the first thing that comes to most peoples minds is Pern. Even if they haven't read it. I've been hearing about the Pern books for as long as I've been reading those genres. I can remember looking at the books in the library as a kid and picking them up from shelves in bookstores but for some reason I never read a single one.<br /><br />With this year being about challenging my reading habits and having to choose something for fantasy I thought it high time</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5221584678807613311">When something mentions fantasy/sci-fi and dragons the first thing that comes to most peoples minds is Pern. Even if they haven't read it. I've been hearing about the Pern books for as long as I've been reading those genres. I can remember looking at the books in the library as a kid and picking them up from shelves in bookstores but for some reason I never read a single one.<br /><br />With this year being about challenging my reading habits and having to choose something for fantasy I thought it high time I actually read a Pern book. And there's nowhere better to start than the beginning.<br /><br />Originally conceived as a couple short stories that went on to win awards McCaffrey pulled 3 short stories together plus a bit of writing between the gaps and Dragonflight was born. So far the Pern books have continued on for another 22 novels and a couple short story collections.<br /><br />But after reading Dragonflight I just think really? I really liked the concept. A strange planet where people and dragons fight this mysterious infestation that only occurs every 200 years (sometimes longer) and lasts around 60 years each time. But the execution was lacking. I think Lessa could have been a much better character. She started out as a strong, intelligent woman but by the end of the book was treated as a stupid, unthinking girl. She has to be controlled by the male Weyrleader. For a book written by the first woman to ever win a major sci-fi/fantasy award she doesn't really treat the female characters that well. Lessa was a virgin who was practically raped (the male character even says it was pretty much that) yet she never mentions it at all. There are at this point only 3 other female characters who have any lines. One dies at the start, one is the wise woman in charge of the stores of the Weyr (cliche much?) and the other is a slut. <br /><br />The ending was frustrating. Cliffhanger of course. After a very long setup the last part of the book, the bit you've been waiting for, just ends without getting to the good parts. After the way the book went I honestly don't think I want to keep reading the Pern books. Disappointing for a book so many people seem to love but it just goes to show again there's no accounting for taste.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5221584678807613311">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy" class="left imgcol" title="Jenny (Reading Envy)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1352348574p2/68030.jpg" alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/574445590?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 31, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy" class="user" title="Jenny (Reading Envy)">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenny (Reading Envy) by: </span>
      Veronica Belmont 
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=sword-and-laser" class="actionLinkLite">sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=hugo-winners-or-nominees" class="actionLinkLite">hugo-winners-or-nominees</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=nebula-winners-or-nominees" class="actionLinkLite">nebula-winners-or-nominees</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2013" class="actionLinkLite">read2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer574445590">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16069054016461270689">This is the April pick for the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser">Sword and Laser</a> book club. I found it as an ebook through my local library's holdings and zipped through it this weekend. <br /><br />This is clearly a book I probably would have connected with more if I'd first read it as a youngling, before I was old and jaded about dragons and romance. I can see how this book set many things for the dragon-and-rider subgenre, alongside dragonrider-dragonrider romance. The story is interesting, especially the somewhat complicated social code</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16069054016461270689">This is the April pick for the <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser">Sword and Laser</a> book club. I found it as an ebook through my local library's holdings and zipped through it this weekend. <br /><br />This is clearly a book I probably would have connected with more if I'd first read it as a youngling, before I was old and jaded about dragons and romance. I can see how this book set many things for the dragon-and-rider subgenre, alongside dragonrider-dragonrider romance. The story is interesting, especially the somewhat complicated social codes and the intricacies of the <em>between</em>.<br /><br />A few examples of what makes this such a representative/leading work:<br /><br />"She would have to be extraordinarily wary. Dragonriders were men apart. Anger did not cloud their intelligence. Greed did not sully their judgment. Fear did not dull their reactions."<br /><br />"The dragon reflected its rider as much the rider the dragon."<br /><br />The one moment that I found moving despite myself was the first connection between Lessa and Ramoth (her dragon) - that was well written and emotional, and I marked it to make sure I said so. And while I don't expect I'll read any further than book 1 in the series, I suspect there could be consequences to what happened in this book, and many more stories to tell. (I notice one is called <a title="The Dolphins of Pern (Pern, #13) by Anne McCaffrey" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127567.The_Dolphins_of_Pern__Pern___13_">The Dolphins of Pern</a>, hmmm.....)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16069054016461270689">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_153908721">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153908721" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3973919-corinne" class="left imgcol" title="Corinne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1281935101p2/3973919.jpg" alt="Corinne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/153908721?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3973919-corinne" class="user" title="Corinne">Corinne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3973919-corinne?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3973919-corinne?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer153908721">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16064434943195219562">Dragonflight takes you through Lessa's journey into the world of dragon riding in Pern. The book lacked character development and I barely connected with the main characters, let along the dozens of bizarre names that would fly by. I read this as an e-book and at the end there was probably 15 pages just explaining terms and who is who (would have been helpful to know earlier...). While those things can be great, as a reader I shouldn't NEED those, the protagonists journey should suffice in intro</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16064434943195219562">Dragonflight takes you through Lessa's journey into the world of dragon riding in Pern. The book lacked character development and I barely connected with the main characters, let along the dozens of bizarre names that would fly by. I read this as an e-book and at the end there was probably 15 pages just explaining terms and who is who (would have been helpful to know earlier...). While those things can be great, as a reader I shouldn't NEED those, the protagonists journey should suffice in introducing you to most new concepts and people. Weak on overall world building.<br /><br />The main enemy of the book was actually a natural disaster that happens (biological matter called Threads fall through the sky). It was an interesting idea, but again the book had one less character you could hate. Perhaps Lessa's abusive boyfriend counts as the antagonist...<br /><br />Props to some of the interesting time traveling that McCaffrey created. It definitely created some creative solutions to problems. <br /><br />It took me a long time to get into this book, I felt like I was out of the loop a lot of the time and never connected with the characters. I am in no rush to read McCaffrey again, I don't really care what happens next. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16064434943195219562">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1462364-anila" class="user" title="Anila">Anila</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer33269603">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3332938735958432070">I'm going to drop a quick note here because I've been thinking about it, but I haven't read this book recently enough to write a real review.<br /><br /><br />This book is the most out of whack with the rest of its series. Here, there is no pretense of science fiction, whereas as the series progresses it is clear that McCaffrey made a decision to change genres. Fencing appears nowhere else in the books, and the implication that Lessa was somehow protected by a magical connection with her Hold is never brought up</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3332938735958432070">I'm going to drop a quick note here because I've been thinking about it, but I haven't read this book recently enough to write a real review.<br /><br /><br />This book is the most out of whack with the rest of its series. Here, there is no pretense of science fiction, whereas as the series progresses it is clear that McCaffrey made a decision to change genres. Fencing appears nowhere else in the books, and the implication that Lessa was somehow protected by a magical connection with her Hold is never brought up again. It's actually a poor starting point for a new reader, since in context of the other books it makes very little sense, but if you're familiar with the later, more normalized Pern, it's very interesting. This is, in all seriousness, the planet at its most fucked up. Spoilers prevent me from explaining it, but things have gone way, way, way wrong and anywhere else in the chronology, they're better. There's probably a message to be imagined here about the importance of history, maybe, but that's not the first purpose of this book. It makes no pretense, by the way, that its purpose is anything but entertainment first, and entertainment in a pulpy sort of fashion that's really quite fun if you're in the right mood for it.<br /><br />Also, there are dragons. Maybe you haven't figured that one out yet? The title is pretty unclear about it, I know.<br /><br />But dragons make everything better, always.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3332938735958432070">...more</a>
