<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_15103458">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15103458" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/895115-veronica-belmont" class="left imgcol" title="Veronica Belmont"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442972647p2/895115.jpg" alt="Veronica Belmont" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15103458?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/895115-veronica-belmont" class="user" title="Veronica Belmont">Veronica Belmont</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/895115-veronica-belmont?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/895115-veronica-belmont?shelf=sword-and-laser" class="actionLinkLite">sword-and-laser</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15103458">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12562100756191184535">I took this review from a 5-star to a 4-star in my rereading. It's Dragonflight still an excellent book? Yes. But perhaps I read now with more of a critical eye than I did almost 20 years ago.<br /><br />The Chronicles of Pern contain some of the most believable and relatable dragons in fantasy, and they're truly the mold from which other dragons in the genre are cut. However, I find my issues now revolve around the human characters in the story. <br /><br />Lessa and F'lar, specifically, seem pulled from a YA novel of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12562100756191184535">I took this review from a 5-star to a 4-star in my rereading. It's Dragonflight still an excellent book? Yes. But perhaps I read now with more of a critical eye than I did almost 20 years ago.<br /><br />The Chronicles of Pern contain some of the most believable and relatable dragons in fantasy, and they're truly the mold from which other dragons in the genre are cut. However, I find my issues now revolve around the human characters in the story. <br /><br />Lessa and F'lar, specifically, seem pulled from a YA novel of today. This isn't really meant to be a YA book, of course. But Lessa's incessant need to prove herself (and to whom, exactly? She was chosen) and F'lar's incessant need to... well, *shake* Lessa, grew tiresome (and even became a point of humor towards the end of the book, so many this was intended).<br /><br />It's a book very much of it's time. It can also err on the side of the cheesy:<br /><br /><em>Mother of us all, he was glad that now, of all times conceivable, he, F’lar, rider of bronze Mnementh, was a dragonman of Pern!</em><br /><br />The best part of the book, in my opinion, is the way McCaffrey deals with time travel. It's never an easy topic to deal with, but the entire setup comes together perfectly at the end of the tale. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12562100756191184535">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254328953" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci" class="left imgcol" title="Ricky Ganci"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428183782p2/5628971.jpg" alt="Ricky Ganci" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/254328953?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci" class="user" title="Ricky Ganci">Ricky Ganci</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer254328953">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7197437043452799990">Well, it was better than Eragon. This is a very cool book—a welcome literary repast. Upon reading the introduction, I thought it was going to be hard fantasy-laced science fiction, but then it settled nicely into being a very traditional fantasy setting. Other newer series that I’ve read seem to draw much from the set up of McCaffrey’s Pern, and the Hold system, complete with Craftmasters, seems to indicate more than a little inspiration to Ranger’s Apprentice. The traditional medieval setting s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7197437043452799990">Well, it was better than Eragon. This is a very cool book—a welcome literary repast. Upon reading the introduction, I thought it was going to be hard fantasy-laced science fiction, but then it settled nicely into being a very traditional fantasy setting. Other newer series that I’ve read seem to draw much from the set up of McCaffrey’s Pern, and the Hold system, complete with Craftmasters, seems to indicate more than a little inspiration to Ranger’s Apprentice. The traditional medieval setting seemed very authentic and manageable to the reader—it didn’t require a study of hours to be familiar with the workings of the story. I like how she starts us off with one Weyr and graduates us to multiple by the end of the book. One thing I was not prepared for was the time-travel aspect. Though the concept of between seems a bit less defined than, say, Card’s philotic explanations, the story is more about Lessa and her growth into a Weyrwoman, her strange but ever-developing relationship with F’lar, and her dragon, Ramoth. The between notion is something that dragons can do, and it works for the reader to simply accept it. There were parts at which the story got away from the dragon-riders, but those few slow and unengaging spots could not detract from the overall quality of the tale. I see now the attraction to Pern by Paolini, whose three chief sources of influence I am now familiar with. Its great source material, and the best fantasy I’ve read since The Name of the Wind last February.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7197437043452799990">...more</a>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Stephenie Meyer</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=fiction-scifi-fantasy-paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-scifi-fantasy-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78107845">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8250345413867088494">This book was good. Adequate might be an even better adjective. <br /><br />In fact, my husband asked if I wanted to go to the bookstore to buy the next book. (He is a very good husband who has continually witnessed me get sucked into fantasy series.) My answer was "huh, it never even crossed my mind to continue the series." One book was enough. I'm glad I read it for a bit of enjoyment and to sample McCaffrey's writing, but I am done. <br /><br />I liked the use of dragons, but the author didn't offer anything new to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8250345413867088494">This book was good. Adequate might be an even better adjective. <br /><br />In fact, my husband asked if I wanted to go to the bookstore to buy the next book. (He is a very good husband who has continually witnessed me get sucked into fantasy series.) My answer was "huh, it never even crossed my mind to continue the series." One book was enough. I'm glad I read it for a bit of enjoyment and to sample McCaffrey's writing, but I am done. <br /><br />I liked the use of dragons, but the author didn't offer anything new to the dragon canon. The world she created has some interesting characteristics, but it wasn't rich enough for me. I liked the two main characters, F'lar and Lessa, but I didn't connect to them as much as I'd prefer. I grew to like and understand their relationship, but their initial coupling was rather disturbing. The plot set a healthy pace, but it was perhaps too brisk and skipped over some potentially interesting scenes. The threat to the planet was scary, but only as scary as spores can get. The ending was clever, but it was also predictable. <br /><br />Overall, it was a enjoyable and quick read. Yet, I would stop short of recommending it to others.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_567214669">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567214669" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="left imgcol" title="Rob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" alt="Rob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/567214669?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10743961-rob" class="user" title="Rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sword-and-laser" class="actionLinkLite">sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013" class="actionLinkLite">read-2013</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer567214669">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16225214593170430638">As I did not particularly care for this book, I'm forgoing the usual format and just writing a quick review. I read this book as the April pick for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser">Sword &amp; Laser</a>. I was vaguely aware of it being considered one of the "classics" of fantasy. It hadn't really been on my radar as something I wanted to read.<br /><br />In fact I had this feeling (based partially on discussing it with a friend who just read it for the first time recently) that I wasn't going to like it, so I borrowed it from the library rathe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16225214593170430638">As I did not particularly care for this book, I'm forgoing the usual format and just writing a quick review. I read this book as the April pick for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser">Sword &amp; Laser</a>. I was vaguely aware of it being considered one of the "classics" of fantasy. It hadn't really been on my radar as something I wanted to read.<br /><br />In fact I had this feeling (based partially on discussing it with a friend who just read it for the first time recently) that I wasn't going to like it, so I borrowed it from the library rather than just buying it like I normally would. Maybe I was setting myself up to dislike it. Either way I'm glad I didn't buy it.<br /><br />I didn't connect to a single human character in the entire book. I found them all to be pretty awful people that I wouldn't want to be around.<br /><br />The only redeeming part of this book to me were the dragons. I think they were well done, and interesting/likable (for dragons). Maybe I'm not being forgiving to the fact the dragonriders themselves are just as arrogant as the dragons they ride.<br /><br />Overall I found the plot lacking too. It seemed to jump all over the place, and when it finally came time to battle the "threads" that threatened Pern, it jumped off again (time travel: go!), then ended rather abruptly. Now I know there are more books, but I can't say I'm really itching to read them.<br /><br />I will say I found the last third or so of the book much better than the first two-thirds, so really this is maybe a 2.5 for me rather than just a flat 2, but I couldn't give it a 3 after spending so much time looking for excuses not to read it. If it hadn't been a club pick and so short, I might have considered dropping it all together.<br /><br />Maybe this is a book I would have enjoyed as a kid, but it's hard for me to say.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16225214593170430638">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_18329076">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18329076" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1012909-curtiss" class="left imgcol" title="Curtiss"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1229319762p2/1012909.jpg" alt="Curtiss" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/18329076?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1012909-curtiss" class="user" title="Curtiss">Curtiss</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/61975.Dragonflight" title="Paperback 9780345484260" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1012909-curtiss?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1012909-curtiss?shelf=all-time-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer18329076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16510263443445065764">I first read this when it was serialized in Analog Science Fiction/Science Fact magazine way back in 1967; I still have all three issues. Its a story of "revenge served cold" in which the heroine Lessa of Ruatha uses her latent psychic powers to bring about the doom of the man who murdered her entire family when she was just a girl. At a later point in the story we learn how Lessa was warned in time to save herself from also being slaughtered by the renegade Fax.<br /><br />We also learn that Lessa's world</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16510263443445065764">I first read this when it was serialized in Analog Science Fiction/Science Fact magazine way back in 1967; I still have all three issues. Its a story of "revenge served cold" in which the heroine Lessa of Ruatha uses her latent psychic powers to bring about the doom of the man who murdered her entire family when she was just a girl. At a later point in the story we learn how Lessa was warned in time to save herself from also being slaughtered by the renegade Fax.<br /><br />We also learn that Lessa's world faces a deadly peril in the form of alien space-traversing spores called 'threads' which periodically rain down on the planet Pern whenever a rogue planet called the Red Star passes near enough for the threads to make the journey between worlds. This rain of death usually occurs at 200 'turn' intervals, but due to an irregularity in the Red Star's orbit there has been a prolonged interval of 400 years; and it is this prolonged threadfree period which has caused the Pernese to lose faith in their guardians and protectors, the dragonriders who are emotionally/psychically-bonded to their fire-breathing mounts.<br /><br />The dragons and their riders are trained to fight the scourge of thread and otherwise depend for their sustainence on the common people of Pern who live in rockbound holds and pay tribute to the Weyr(s) for their protection. After 400 turns without threadfall, not only have the Pernese lost their belief in thread and their faith in the dragons and their riders, but for some unknown reason all but one dragon Weyr has been abandoned, and the population of dragons for Pern's defense has declined to a barely sustainable level; well below the numbers needed to defend an entire planet.<br /><br />Only F'lar a bronze dragonrider and his brother F'nor a brown rider, truly believe in the impending threat of threadfall. They are on a quest to find a new queen rider to bond with the latest queen egg when it hatches, and visit Ruatha Hold accompanied by the usurper Fax as part of their 'Search' for a likely candidate. Lessa's plans disrupt their visit and nearly cause F'lar's death, but he realizes that she is the source of the disruption and a very promising candidate indeed.<br /><br />F'lar persuades Lessa to leave broken-down Ruatha Hold to the new heir and instead try to 'Impress' the new queen dragon egg when it hatches. Lessa's latent psychic power becomes fully actualized when she and the new queen, Ramoth form a bond during the 'impression' ceremony. Lessa becomes the queen dragonrider, and Weyrwoman as the co-leader of Pern's last remaining Weyr. The leadership of the Weyr is determined by which bronze dragon mates with the queen dragon when it 'rises' on its mating flight. During this flight, the psychic bond between the dragons and their riders produces a frenzy which leads to mutual sexual consummation between both the pair of mating dragons and their two dragonriders. <br /><br />Many comments characterize this sexual frenzy as 'rape' and even F'lar acknowledges that without Lessa's emotional bond-induced response to Ramoth's mating flight it might as well BE rape. On the other hand, Lessa accepted the job of Weyrwoman in the full knowledge of what the sexual relationships within the Weyr were or were rumored to be. And in the context of providing the ultimate protection of an entire planet, the dragonriders have made lifestyle commitments that may seem objectionable to some. After all the other riders are all male and are bonded to brown and blue male dragons or to green female dragons which still engage in mating activities even though their fire-breathing diet prevents the greens from laying viable eggs. These guys must do to 'something' to relieve their own dragon-induced frenzy.<br /><br />As for F'lar's 'physical abuse' of Lessa by shaking her; Lessa's egocentric behavior jeopardizes the life of the last remaining queen dragon, the only dragon on Pern capable of laying viable eggs with which to rebuild the defenses of the entire planet! She darn well deserves a good shaking! Especially after the first threadfall occurs and proves F'lar was right about the danger of the current Red Star's pass.<br /><br />The other harsh aspects of Pernese culture all derive from the fundamental dilemma they all face as the survivors of a nearly-failed colony whose space-travelling technology has been all but wiped-out by the deadly threads from the Red Planet. Pern is facing a threat to its very existence and civilization has reverted to more primitive values and mores, including a feudal culture with guilds to preserve the remnants of technology, arranged marriages (in essence a form of rape, right?), and tribute paid to a cadre of defenders with military organization and traditions.<br /><br />Fortunately for Pern, Lessa and Ramoth accidentally discover that in addition to the ability to instantaneously teleport or fly 'between' places to any spot on Pern that the dragonrider can visualize (a tremendous help in combating threadfall), the dragon's can also fly between TIMES, which allows F'lar to plan sweeps to combat threadfall at earlier times and places to maximize the fighting power of his dragons and riders. Despite this the few remaining dragon's in Pern's last Weyr find themselves overstretched and unable to meet the demands of fighting threadfall over the entire planet.<br /><br />Lessa becomes obsessed with the disturbing lyrics of 'The Question Song' which refers to the disappearance of the dragons and riders from the other Weyrs, and is convinced that somehow those dragons came forward through time to help fight threadfall during the Red Star's current pass. She also becomes convinced someone had to have gone back in time 400 turns to bring them forward, and she knows of a tapestry in Ruatha Hold which was created at that previous time, with such a wealth of detail in its weaving that she, Lessa, could use that detail to focus on Ruatha at that moment in time. This leads her to make an epic flight 'between times' to bring the other Weyrs forward to assist in Pern's defense, because after all, as the dragonrider's creed says:<br /><br />"Dragons must fly, when thread is in the sky."<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16510263443445065764">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14522736749001567421">I really enjoyed this book. The first 20 pages were completely confusing and I couldn't figure out what anything meant: weyr, between, watch-wher, hold? And the names in the book were so weird: F'lar, Mnementh, F'nor... But I'm glad I kept reading. After about 20 pages I started to love this book. Despite having little time to devote to reading I finished it in less than 3 days.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6264813426665415293">I liked the first book in the series a lot. Well crafted characters, customs, and world. It is also refreshingly clean. There is no smut or crap to wade through to find a delightful story line. A must for the well read fantasy aficionado. This story that kept coming back to me, taunting me. I mean really... what fantasy nut doesn't want to ride a dragon?</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1182136355">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1182136355" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1200744-aldi" class="left imgcol" title="Aldi"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1392344034p2/1200744.jpg" alt="Aldi" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1182136355?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1200744-aldi" class="user" title="Aldi">Aldi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1996409.Dragonflight" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345284266" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1200744-aldi?shelf=dragons-dragons-dragons" class="actionLinkLite">dragons-dragons-dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1182136355">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15222522431183075856">Good fun! I never realised there was a time-travel element to these as well - I love a good intricate time travel plot, and this was very nicely done. And the world-building, history and sci-fi background was really well-crafted - I particularly enjoyed spotting things that later fantasy authors clearly <s>stole</s> <s>heavily borrowed</s> paid loving homage to ;) It felt a bit like reading an origin myth for many of my favourite fantasy universes. <br /><br />Character-wise, it was a great relief to have a female main c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15222522431183075856">Good fun! I never realised there was a time-travel element to these as well - I love a good intricate time travel plot, and this was very nicely done. And the world-building, history and sci-fi background was really well-crafted - I particularly enjoyed spotting things that later fantasy authors clearly <s>stole</s> <s>heavily borrowed</s> paid loving homage to ;) It felt a bit like reading an origin myth for many of my favourite fantasy universes. <br /><br />Character-wise, it was a great relief to have a female main character who was neither given to helpless damselling nor the typical rebellious princess stereotype. I adore scratchy heroines with plenty of flaws, and Lessa fit that bill perfectly while still being very much unique (again, saw some inspiration there for some of my favourite scifi/fantasy heroines in later works!). I do hope for lots more self-empowerment from her, though, and on a related note, I'm really not a fan of F'lar so far - too much smug superiority, too much condescension and chuckling (I loathe men who chuckle :p) and above all, ENOUGH WITH THE BLOODY SHAKING! Asserting physical dominance over a woman is not funny or endearing or an acceptable expression of concern! Stop shaking her, you bloody prick! Blergh.<br /><br />I did love F'nor and am curious about some of the other characters - so far there hasn't been that much development or focus on anyone but the main chars but I am intrigued.<br /><br />Loved the dragons, too! They should just take over rule of the world, as they're clearly the more sensible of the two species, lol. <br /><br />(Side note: The naming conventions. No. If you have a two-syllable name and you replace one vowel with an apostrophe, you STILL HAVE A TWO-SYLLABLE NAME. It doesn't shorten anything and it looks daft. Admittedly, I have been put off fantasy names with apostrophes by ample abuse of same by later authors). <br /><br />As for the writing, I struggled a bit at times, because it's so sparse as to almost be perfunctory - sometimes you miss a major event if you blink or start turning the page too soon because it's so exposition-heavy. It made for an interesting counter-point to modern fantasy, though, which is sometimes so very detailed and/or trying for lyrical that it's almost too much. I do tend to prioritize good characters and a good story over good writing, and this had both of those, so it's all good. It definitely sets up a fantastic canvas for future adventures and I'll definitely read at least the other books of the primary series.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15222522431183075856">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

Since leaving Darkover as a child, Margaret had lived her life on Thetis. Lew and her stepmother, Diotima, were gone much of the year, working in the Senate, struggling to keep Darkover safe from the all-consuming imperialism of the Terran Federation. She hardly knew her father, a brooding man who, when he returned to Thetis, was prone to long bouts of drinking. At these times, his normally morose and uncommunicative demeanor would take on an even darker hue ... times when he seemed to look at Margaret and see someone else - someone he did not want to remember. As soon as Margaret was of age, she fled her stormy home and took refuge on University. Here Margaret, strangely uncomfortable around her peers, found solace in the isolation of study. She excelled in music and was granted the position of assistant to her mentor, renowned musicologist Dr. Ivor Davidson. This prestigious job took her to many worlds, and when she and Professor Davidson were assigned to collect folk songs on Darkover, Margaret was curious and pleased. But once on Darkover, Margaret\'s innocent excitement quickly waned. The world of her birth evoked long-buried memories, painful and terrifying, and she soon found herself falling deeper and deeper into a waking dream that threatened to become a nightmare.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">About Anne McCaffrey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey"><img alt="26" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1323715139p2/26.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer13124324303385256523">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts, at 1:30 p.m., in the hour of the Sheep, year of the Fire Tiger, sun sign Aries with Taurus rising and Leo mid-heaven (which seems to suggest an early interest in the stars).<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13124324303385256523">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts, at 1:30 p.m., in the hour of the Sheep, year of the Fire Tiger, sun sign Aries with Taurus rising and Leo mid-heaven (which seems to suggest an early interest in the stars).<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/">Locus</a>, <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13124324303385256523">...more</a>

    </div>

</a>

In exchange for sanctuary in the huge stone fortresses, the people tithed to their Lord Holders, who in turn supported the Weyrs, whose dragons were Pern\'s greatest weapon against Thread.But not everyone on Pern was part of that system of mutual care and protection, particularly those who had been rendered holdless as punishment for wrongdoing. And there were some, like Jayge\'s trader clan, who simply preferred the freedom of the roads to the security of a hold. Others, like Aramina\'s family, had lost their holds through injustice and cruelty. For all the holdless, life was a constant struggle for survival.\n\nThen, from the ranks of the criminals and the disaffected, rose a band of renegades, led by the Lady Thella. No one was safe from Thella\'s depredations, and now her quarry was Aramina, reputed to have a telepathic link with dragons. But when Thella mistakenly vented her rage on Jayge\'s family, she made a dangerous mistake.
